       if (protocol == RebalanceProtocol.COOPERATIVE) {\n422:             SortedSet<TopicPartition> revokedPartitions = new TreeSet<>(COMPARATOR);\n423:             revokedPartitions.addAll(ownedPartitions);\n424:             revokedPartitions.removeAll(assignedPartitions);\n425: \n426:             log.info(\"Updating assignment with\\n\" +\n427:                     \"\\tAssigned partitions:                       {}\\n\" +\n428:                     \"\\tCurrent owned partitions:                  {}\\n\" +\n429:                     \"\\tAdded partitions // Revoke partitions that were previously owned but no longer assigned;\n439:                 // note that we should only change the assignment (or update the assignor's state)\n440:                 // AFTER we've triggered  the revoke callback\n441:                 firstException.compareAndSet(null, rebalanceListenerInvoker.invokePartitionsRevoked(revokedPartitions));\n442: \n443:         \"by the current assignment and re-join\", revokedPartitions);\n446:                 requestRejoin(\"need to revoke partitions and re-join\", fullReason);\n447:             }\n448:         }\n449: \n450:         // The leader may have assigned partitions which match our subscription pattern, but which\n451:         // were not explicitly requested, so we update the joined subscription here.\n452:         maybeUpdateJoinedSubscription(assignedPartitions);\n453: \n454:         // Catch any exception here to make sure we could complete the user callback.\n455:         firstException.compareAndSet(null, invokeOnAssignment(assignor, assignment));\n456: \n457:         // Reschedule the auto commit starting from now\n458:         if (autoCommitEnabled)\n459: previously owned but are now assigned\n464:         firstException.compareAndSet(null, rebalanceListenerInvoker.invokePartitionsAssigned(addedPartitions));\n465: \n466:         if (firstException.get() != null) {\n467:             if (firstException.get() instanceof KafkaException) {\n468:                 throw (KafkaException) firstException.get();\n469:             } else {\n470:                 throw new KafkaException(\"User rebalance callback throws an error\", firstException.get());\n471:             }\n472:         }\n473:     }\n474: \n475:     void snapshot, which will be used to check for subscription\n484:             // changes that would require a rebalance (e.g. new partitions).\n485:             metadataSnapshot = new coordinatorUnknown() && !ensureCoordinatorReady(timer);\n491:     }\n492: \n493:     private boolean coordinatorUnknownAndUnreadyAsync() {\n494:         return coordinatorUnknown() && !ensureCoordinatorReadyAsync();\n495:     }\n496: \n497:     /**\n498:      * Poll for coordinator events. This ensures that the coordinator is known and that the consumer\n499:      * has joined the group (if it is using group management). This also handles periodic offset commits\n500:      * if they are enabled.\n501:      * <p>\n502:      * Returns early if the timeout expires or if waiting on rejoin is not required\n503:      *\n504:      * @param timer Timer bounding how long this method can block\n505:      * @param waitForJoinGroup Boolean flag indicating if we should wait until re-join group completes\n506:      * @throws KafkaException if the rebalance callback throws an exception\n507:      * @return true iff the operation succeeded\n508:      */\n509:     public boolean poll(Timer timer, boolean waitForJoinGroup) {\n510:         maybeUpdateSubscriptionMetadata();\n511: \n512:         invokeCompletedOffsetCommitCallbacks();\n513: \n514:         if (subscriptions.hasAutoAssignedPartitions()) {\n515:             if (protocol == null) {\n516:                 throw new IllegalStateException(\"User configured \" + ConsumerConfig.PARTITION_ASSIGNMENT_STRATEGY_CONFIG +\n517:                     \" to empty while trying to subscribe for group protocol to auto assign partitions\");\n518:             }\n519:             // Always update the heartbeat last poll time so that the heartbeat thread does not leave the\n520:             // group proactively due to application inactivity even if (say) the coordinator cannot be found.\n521:             pollHeartbeat(timer.currentTimeMs());\n522:             if (coordinatorUnknownAndUnreadySync(timer)) {\n523:                 return false;\n524:             }\n525: \n526:             if (rejoinNeededOrPending()) {\n527:                 // due to a race condition between the initial metadata fetch and the initial rebalance,\n528:                 // we need to ensure that the metadata is fresh before joining initially. This ensures\n529:                 // that we have matched the pattern against the cluster's topics at least once before joining.\n530:                 if (subscriptions.hasPatternSubscription()) {\n531:                     // For consumer group that uses pattern-based subscription, after a topic is created,\n532:                     // any consumer that discovers the topic after metadata refresh can trigger rebalance\n533:                     // across the entire consumer group. Multiple rebalances can be triggered after one topic\n534:                     // creation if consumers refresh metadata at vastly different times. We can significantly\n535:                     // reduce the number of rebalances caused by single topic creation by asking consumer to\n536:                     // refresh metadata before re-joining the group as long as the refresh backoff time has\n537:                     // passed.\n538:                     if (this.metadata.timeToAllowUpdate(timer.currentTimeMs()) == 0) {\n539:                         this.metadata.requestUpdate(true);\n540:                     }\n541: \n542:                     if (!client.ensureFreshMetadata(timer)) {\n543:                         return false;\n544:                     }\n545: \n546:                     maybeUpdateSubscriptionMetadata();\n547:                 }\n548: \n549:                 // if not wait for join group, we would just use a timer of 0\n550:                 if (!ensureActiveGroup(waitForJoinGroup ? timer : time.timer(0L))) {\n551:                     // since we may use a different timer in the callee, we'd still need\n552:                     // to update the original timer's current time after the call\n553:                     timer.update(time.milliseconds());\n554: \n555:                     return false;\n556:                 }\n557:             }\n558:         } else {\n559:             // For manually assigned partitions, we do not try to pro-actively lookup coordinator;\n560:             // instead we only try to refresh metadata when necessary.\n561:             // If connections to all nodes fail, wakeups triggered while attempting to send fetch\n562:             // requests result in polls returning immediately, causing a tight loop of polls. Without\n563:             // the wakeup, poll() with no channels would block for the timeout, delaying re-connection.\n564:             // awaitMetadataUpdate() in ensureCoordinatorReady initiates new connections with configured backoff and avoids the busy loop.\n565:             if (metadata.updateRequested() && !client.hasReadyNodes(timer.currentTimeMs())) {\n566:                 client.awaitMetadataUpdate(timer);\n567:             }\n568: \n569:             // if there is pending coordinator requests, ensure they have a chance to be transmitted.\n570:             client.pollNoWakeup();\n571:         }\n572: \n573:         maybeAutoCommitOffsetsAsync(timer.currentTimeMs());\n574:         return true;\n575:     }\n576: \n577:     /**\n578:      * Return the time to the next needed invocation of {@link ConsumerNetworkClient#poll(Timer)}.\n579:      * @param now current time in milliseconds\n580:      * @return the maximum time in milliseconds the caller should wait before the next invocation of poll()\n581:      */\n582:     public long timeToNextPoll(long now) {\n583:         if (!autoCommitEnabled)\n584:             return timeToNextHeartbeat(now);\n585: \n586:         return Math.min(nextAutoCommitTimer.remainingMs(), timeToNextHeartbeat(now));\n587:     }\n588: \n589:     private void updateGroupSubscription(Set<String> topics) {\n590:         // throw new TimeoutException();\n599: \n600:         maybeUpdateSubscriptionMetadata();\n601:     }\n602: \n603:     private boolean isAssignFromSubscribedTopicsAssignor(String name) {\n604:     * and assign their partitions to the members; in this case we would like to update the leader's\n610:      * own metadata with the newly added topics so that it will not trigger a subsequent assignors.\n614:      *\n615:      * TODO: this is a hack and not something we want to support long-term unless we push regex into the protocol\n616:      *       we may need to modify the      * it must first remove it from the new assignment of the current owner so that it is not assigned to any\n720:      * member, and then in the next rebalance it can finally reassign those partitions not owned by anyone to consumers.\n721:      */\n722:     private void validateCooperativeAssignment(final Map<String, List<TopicPartition>> ownedPartitions,\n723:                                                final Map<String, Assignment> assignments) {\n724:         Set<TopicPartition> totalRevokedPartitions = new HashSet<>();\n725:         SortedSet<TopicPartition> entry.getValue();\n728:             final Set<TopicPartition> addedPartitions = new HashSet<>(assignment.partitions());\n729: private void maybeMarkPartitionsPendingRevocation() {\n865:         if (protocol != RebalanceProtocol.EAGER) {\n866:             return;\n867:         }\n868: \n869:         // When asynchronously committing offsets prior to the revocation of a set of partitions, there will be a\n870:         // window of time between when the offset commit is sent and when it returns and revocation completes. It is\n871:         // possible for pending fetches for these partitions to return during this time, which means the application's\n872:         // position may get ahead of the committed position prior to revocation. This can cause duplicate consumption.\n873:         // To prevent this, we mark the partitions as \"pending revocation,\" which stops the Fetcher from sending new\n874:         // fetches or returning {}\", partitions);\n877:         subscriptions.markPendingRevocation(partitions);\n878:     }\n879: \n880:     @Override\n881:     public void onLeavePrepare() {\n882:         // Save the current @Override\n913:     public boolean rejoinNeededOrPending() {\n914:         if (!subscriptions.hasAutoAssignedPartitions())\n915:             return false;\n916: \n917:         // we need to rejoin if                            final Timer timer) {\n963:         if (partitions.isEmpty()) return Collections.emptyMap();\n964: \n965:         final Generation generationForOffsetRequest =   // if we were waiting for a different request, then just clear it.\n969:             pendingCommittedOffsetRequest = null;\n970:         }\n971: \n972:         long attempts = 0L;\n973:         do {\n974:             if (!ensureCoordinatorReady(timer)) return null;\n975: \n976:             // contact coordinator to fetch committed offsets\n977:             final RequestFuture<Map<TopicPartition, OffsetAndMetadata>> future;\n978:             if (pendingCommittedOffsetRequest != null) {\n979:                 future = pendingCommittedOffsetRequest.response;\n980:             } else {\n981:                 future = sendOffsetFetchRequest(partitions);\n982:                 pendingCommittedOffsetRequest = new    }\n996:             } else {\n997:                 return null;\n998:             }\n999:         } while (timer.notExpired());\n1000:         return null;\n1001:     }\n1002: \n1003:       super.close(timer, membershipOperation);\n1027:         }\n1028:     }\n1029: \n1030:     // visible for testing\n1031:     void invokeCompletedOffsetCommitCallbacks() {\n1032:         if callback) {\n1047:         invokeCompletedOffsetCommitCallbacks();\n1048: \n1049:         RequestFuture<Void> future = null;\n1050:         if (offsets.isEmpty()) {\n1051:             // No need to check coordinator if offsets is empty since commit of empty offsets is completed locally.\n1052:             future = doCommitOffsetsAsync(offsets, callback);\n1053:         } else if (!coordinatorUnknownAndUnreadyAsync()) {\n1054:             // we need to make sure coordinator is ready before committing, since\n1055:             // this is for async committing we do not try to block, but just try once to\n1056:             // clear the previous discover-coordinator future, resend, or get responses;\n1057:             // if the coordinator is not ready yet then we would just proceed and put that into the\n1058:             // pending requests, and future poll calls would still try to complete them.\n1059:             //\n1060:             // the key here though is that we have to try sending the discover-coordinator if\n1061:             // it's not known or ready, since this is the only place we can send such request\n1062:             // under manual assignment (there we would not have heartbeat thread trying to auto-rediscover\n1063:             // the coordinator).\n1064:             future = doCommitOffsetsAsync(offsets, callback);\n1065:         } else {\n1066:             // we don't know the current coordinator, so try to find it and then send the commit\n1067:             // or fail (we don't want recursive retries which can cause offset commits to arrive\n1068:             // out of order). Note that there may be multiple offset commits chained to the same\n1069:             // coordinator lookup request. This is fine because the listeners will be invoked in\n1070:             // the same order that they were added. Note also that AbstractCoordinator prevents\n1071:             // multiple concurrent coordinator lookup requests.\n1072:             pendingAsyncCommits.incrementAndGet();\n1073:             lookupCoordinator().addListener(new RequestFutureListener<>() {\n1074:                 @Override\n1075:                 public void onSuccess(Void value) {\n1076:                     pendingAsyncCommits.decrementAndGet();\n1077:                     doCommitOffsetsAsync(offsets, callback);\n1078:                     client.pollNoWakeup();\n1079:                 }\n1080: \n1081:                 @Override\n1082:                 public void onFailure(RuntimeException e) {\n1083:                     pendingAsyncCommits.decrementAndGet();\n1084:                     completedOffsetCommits.add(new OffsetCommitCompletion(callback, offsets,\n1085:                             new RetriableCommitFailedException(e)));\n1086:                 }\n1087:             });\n1088:         }\n1089: \n1090:         // ensure the commit has a chance to be transmitted (without blocking on its completion).\n1091:         // Note that commits are treated as heartbeats by the coordinator, so there is no need to\n1092:         // explicitly allow heartbeats through delayed task execution.\n1093:         client.pollNoWakeup();\n1094:         return future;\n1095:     }\n1096: \n1097:     private RequestFuture<Void> doCommitOffsetsAsync(final Map<TopicPartition, OffsetAndMetadata> offsets, final OffsetCommitCallback callback) {\n1098:         RequestFuture<Void> future = sendOffsetCommitRequest(offsets);\n1099:         inFlightAsyncCommits.incrementAndGet();\n1100:         final OffsetCommitCallback cb = callback == null ? subscriptions.allConsumed();\n1181:             try {\n1182:                 log.debug(\"Sending synchronous auto-commit of offsets {}\", allConsumedOffsets);\n1183:                 if }\n1195: \n1196:     public void maybeAutoCommitOffsetsAsync(long now) {\n1197:         if (autoCommitEnabled) {\n1198:             nextAutoCommitTimer.update(now);\n1199:             if @Override\n1254:         public void onComplete(Map<TopicPartition, OffsetAndMetadata> offsets, Exception exception) {\n1255:             if (exception != null)\n1256: ConsumerCoordinator.commitOffsetsSync()\\nCore synchronous commit logic at `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/internals/ConsumerCoordinator.java:1140-1176`. This method:\\n- Invokes pending offset commit callbacks\\n- Calls `sendOffsetCommitRequest()` to send the actual request to the coordinator\\n- Polls the client until the response is received or timeout occurs\\n- Throws CommitFailedException or RebalanceInProgressException on unrecoverable errors\\n\\n### 4. ConsumerCoordinator.sendOffsetCommitRequest()\\nImplementation at `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/internals/ConsumerCoordinator.java:1270-1343`. This method:\\n- Constructs an OffsetCommitRequest containing the offsets to commit\\n- Includes groupId, memberId, generation ID, and the TopicPartition->OffsetAndMetadata mappings\\n- Sends the request to the group coordinator broker via `client.send()`\\n- Registers an OffsetCommitResponseHandler to process the response\\n\\n## Broker-Side Flow\\n\\n### 5. KafkaApis.handleOffsetCommitRequest()\\nBroker request handler at `core/src/main/scala/kafka/server/KafkaApis.scala:272-365`. This method:\\n- Receives the OffsetCommitRequest from the network\\n- Performs authorization checks (verifies read access to the group)\\n- Filters topics by authorization (TOPIC resource)\\n- Resolves topic IDs to names if needed\\n- Delegates to `groupCoordinator.commitOffsets()` for the actual offset commit\\n\\n### 6. GroupCoordinatorService.commitOffsets()\\nCoordinator service entry point at `group-coordinator/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/coordinator/group/GroupCoordinatorService.java:1971-2002`. This method:\\n- Validates that the coordinator is active\\n- Calls `runtime.scheduleWriteOperation()` to schedule a write operation on the coordinator\\n- The operation will be executed by a coordinator shard, which will process the commit and write to the log\\n- Returns a CompletableFuture that completes when the write is done\\n\\n### 7. This method:\\n- Validates the offset commit request (checks authorization, metadata size)\\n- For classic groups, reschedules member heartbeats if the group is in STABLE or PREPARING_REBALANCE state\\n- Creates an OffsetCommitResponseData for the response\\n- For each topic and partition in the request, creates a CoordinatorRecord using `GroupCoordinatorRecordHelpers.newOffsetCommitRecord()`\\n- Returns a CoordinatorResult containing the records to be written and the response data\\n\\n### 9. GroupCoordinatorRecordHelpers.newOffsetCommitRecord()\\nRecord creation at `group-coordinator/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/coordinator/group/GroupCoordinatorRecordHelpers.java:467-491`. This method:\\n- Creates an OffsetCommitKey with the groupId, topic, and partition\\n- Creates an OffsetCommitValue containing:\\n  - The committed offset\\n  - Leader epoch\\n  - Metadata\\n  - Commit timestamp\\n  - Expiration timestamp (for TTL-based retention)\\n  - Topic ID\\n- Wraps these in a CoordinatorRecord with the appropriate version\\n\\n## Log Append\\n\\nThe CoordinatorRecord objects created above are then appended to the __consumer_offsets topic by the coordinator runtime. The actual log append is handled by:\\n- `CoordinatorRuntime.scheduleWriteOperation()` which manages the write to the underlying Kafka log\\n- The records are written to the __consumer_offsets topic partition that corresponds to the group's partition (calculated via hash of groupId)\\n- The operation ensures all in-sync replicas acknowledge the write before returning success to the client\\n\\n## Summary\\n\\nThe flow creates a chain of responsibility from the consumer application to the persistent __consumer_offsets topic:\\n1. Consumer calls commitSync() on KafkaConsumer\\n2. Request is routed through ClassicKafkaConsumer -> ConsumerCoordinator\\n3. OffsetCommitRequest is sent to the group coordinator broker\\n4. Broker validates and routes through KafkaApis -> GroupCoordinatorService\\n5. Coordinator shard processes via OffsetMetadataManager\\n6. Offset commit records are created and appended to __consumer_offsets log\\n7.
